Geotechnical Engineering Construction Services
Mass Grading Observation and Testing
Kapolei Knolls Phase 2 Subdivision
16 115
Kapolei Oahu Hawaii
Grading Permit No
Dear Ms Seddon
This report summarizes our geotechnical engineering observations performed
during the mass grading pad grading utility installation and road construction operations
from May 2002 to February 2004 for the above project in accordance with our fee proposal
dated May 10 2001
Project Considerations
The project consists of a single family residential subdivision with 212 lots and four
roads It is anticipated that the residences will consist of light one and two story structures
The four roads have an aggregate length of about 5 000Linear Feet LF To
accommodate grade differences retaining walls that retain up to 10 feet of backfill were
necessary for some of the lots in the subdivision Infrastructure including sidewalks and
utilities were also constructed for the project
The mass grading work involved about 158 000 cubic yards of fill and about
148 000 cubic yards of cuts These amounts do not account for soil shrinkage due to
compaction or loss of material from clearing and grubbing The mass grading work
generally consisted of cuts and fills less than 15 feet to create terraces of lots that slope
downward towards the south
Site Grading
The earthwork operations for the project were performed by Royal Contracting
Company At the on set of earthwork areas within the contract grading limits were
generally cleared and grubbed of vegetation and deleterious materials Materials
generated from the clearing operations were disposed of off site Following the clearing
and grubbing operations the areas to be cut were excavated Finish grades were
compacted using a sheeps foot and or smooth drum vibratory roller
2006 Kalihi Street Honolulu Hawaii 96819
Hawaii California
6
Schuler Homes Inc Page 2
In general on site soil materials generated from the excavation were primarily used
in the deeper fill area The on site fill materials generally consisted of silty and clayey soils
with some gravel The expansion of the on site fill material ranged from low to high
Samples of the fill and backfill materials utilized during construction were obtained and
transported to our office for laboratory testing The maximum dry densities and optimum
moisture contents were established in our laboratory in general accordance with American
Society of Testing and Material ASTM Test Designation D 1557 Modified Proctor The
test results are summarized on Plate 3 of this report
In general the excavated basalt rock was processed through an on site crusher to
produce structural fill generally less than 6 inches in size and was used as structural fill
materials for the top 3 feet of the fill lots Field density tests were performed with the
nuclear density gauge ASTM Test Designations D 2922 and D 3017 During the fill and
backfill operations the materials were generally placed in near level lifts brought to near
the optimum moisture and compacted to obtain the specified degree of compaction based
on visual observations and or field density tests Periodic field density tests were
performed during the fill and backfill operations to confirm our field observations as
variations in construction procedures and soil conditions were noted
Over excavation of about 2 to 3 feet was conducted at the lots where moderately
to highly expansive soil was encountered at the subgrade of the house foundation
Crushed basalt structural fill material was used to backfill these lots
A total of 2 826 field density tests including re tests of failed areas were performed
using the nuclear density gauge method in general accordance with ASTM Test
Designations D 2922 and D 3017 The results of the compaction tests performed during
construction of the above project are summarized on Plates 4 1 through 4 207 of this
report Test locations and elevations were estimated by pacing and interpolating from
on site survey stakes where available These locations and elevations should be
considered accurate only to the degree implied by the methods used
Based on the observations of our field representatives and the results of the
referenced tests it is our professional opinion that the earthwork operations for the Kapolei
Knolls Phase 2 Subdivision project observed and tested by Geolabs in the period covered
by this report were performed in general conformance with the intent of the plans and
specifications and our recommendations In general areas assessed to be
unsatisfactory were re worked to achieve the specified minimum compaction
Additional Recommendations for Homeowner
Homeowners should immediately verify whether their swales have been
compromised or altered from the original condition of initial move in If these swales have
been altered consult your plot plan and reinstall the swales Swales should also be
grassed as leaving them bare will result in soil erosion during heavy rains
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
Schuler Homes Inc Page 3
If the swales can not be completely reinstalled because of constructed wall
obstructions installation of drain pipe along the rear and sides of the property can help
drain excess water away from the sidewalks and building slabs
If a homeowner constructs improvements or expansions beyond the original floor
area for example expanding the lanai adding another 1 floor bedroom or family room
etc the services of a qualified geotechnical engineer should be retained to evaluate the
soil conditions at their respective lot for site specific building recommendations
Limitations
This office assumes no responsibility for any alterations made to slopes or finished
grades on the project subsequent to our observation and testing period without our
knowledge and written acknowledgment Lot owners should be advised not to block the
surface drainage and to obtain professional consultation in the planning design and
construction of any future improvements Lot owners should also be advised not to water
excessively adjacent to the house structure
lt should be noted that it is not possible to continuously observe all activities
occurring simultaneously on a construction site therefore some work may have occurred
without our observation However we believe that the level of earthwork observation and
testing services provided is reasonable in reducing the geotechnical risks to the project It
should be recognized that there are variations in the accuracy and statistical repeatability
of the tests and methods used to monitor the earthwork construction and materials Our
services were performed in accordance with generally accepted standards of geotechnical
engineering practice no warranty is expressed or implied Provision of construction
monitoring by an engineer is not insurance nor does it guarantee construction of any type
The contractor shall retain responsibility for the quality of the work for adhering to the
plans and specifications and for repairing defects
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
Schuler Homes Inc Page 4
Closure
We appreciate the opportunity to be of continued service to you on this project If
you have questions or need additional information please contact our office
Respectfully submitted
